  37. I really liked this product - had a very similar experience to \\"Patent Mom\\" - read her review to understand what to expect. I wanted to help clarify some things about the product that could help you decide if this product is right for you. No, I don't work for the company. I really liked this product, but the chemical smells made me nervous, so I asked my stylist about it. She had some interesting info - I thought it might be helpful to others, as well. This product is similar to home perms from the 80s. The thiol breaks the protein bonds in your hair, and then you use heat to essentially \\"re-set\\" them into the style you want. So, YES - it is a chemical, it does smell, and you need to be careful if you do other things to your hair on a regular basis - it could cause damage. You are essentially \\"perming\\" your hair to be straight. Some suggested things to consider before you buy: 1) How often you do other chemical processes to your hair, and how extreme they are. If you regularly bleach your hair (i.e. you maintain blonde but are naturally a brunette) it's probably best to skip it. If you regularly highlight your hair, you probably want to wait a few weeks before you use this... and then wait a few more weeks before you highlight again. 2) Given that it's a chemical process, consider it a \\"once every 6 months\\" kind of thing, not a \\"once every 6 weeks\\" kind of thing. 3) How prone your hair is to damage, anyway. If you would never chemically straighten your hair, this isn't for you. For best results... PLAN to spend a lot of time on the final step - blowdry and straightening. This is the part where you are telling your hair how you want it to \\"re-set\\" (heat activates the thiol). The more thorough you are in getting your hair perfectly smooth, the better results you will have. I hope that helps!

It felt better when the 2nd product was applied before blowdrying, although my hair felt \\"heavy\\" and a bit \\"sticky\\". My blow dry time was not shortened dramatically - perhaps 15 minutes instead of 20 to straighten my hair. I did not follow up with flatiron until a few hours later. What I noticed during blow dry is that it was much easier to straighten; even without the large round brush I use, I could pull my hair straight with my hands as I got most of the water out, and got it fairly smooth, straight, and dry within 1st 5 minutes of blow dry. I probably could have stopped there & been pretty straight, but I went for the full straightening routine, with round brush & concentrator, to see how good it would look. It looked as straight as my stylist gets it pre-flatiron. The real best part of this product is in the days following blow dry. Each day, even the humid ones, I would wake up up with my hair just as smooth and frizz free as it was when I dried it. I normally wash my hair every 2-3 days, so as of today (8/24), I've washed it twice since applying the product 9 days ago (thus I've not reached 7 shampoos yet) -- am due to wash it today, but it still looks quite nice, honestly. My hair still remains very frizz free and my straightening \\"holds up\\" as well as a salon blow dry. I've gone to the beach, walked in drizzle for a few minutes, been exposed to 100% humidity for past three days - still ZERO frizz since washing it two days ago on a rainy day (followed by blow dry and flatiron). I've been accidentally squirted with water, which normally would cause that section to curl right up, but not after using this product. It still takes nearly 15 minutes to blow dry (using my usual KMS and morrocan oil products), but the results are far straighter, smoother, and shinier than I ever got before. I almost don't need the flatiron. Also, I can get my hair mostly very straight within my initial 5 minutes of blow drying (where I get hair to 80% dry) just by pulling my hair up and out with my hands and moving the dryer nozzle around it. For the last 10 minutes, I use a dryer with a concentrator & round brush, and the results look almost as good as a salon blowout (to me at least). My hair does not feel \\"heavy\\" as it did when I initially applied the 2nd step of this product. I don't understand the comments about this product causing damage. I have processed hair and have seen no damage whatsoever. In fact, my hair seems to look healthier, because it is so frizz free. What I want to know is how frequently I can use it. I definitely plan to use it again. I will post again after I've reached the 7 shampoos, to report on how well the product lasts.

  57. Just a fore-warning. Don't use this product if you've had your hair relaxed with no-lye or lye product in the past year. If your hair is not healthy (and not according to YOUR standard, ask your stylist), don't use this product. If you have wavy hair, don't use product. There's a picture on the back of the box stating what hair you can use it on. USE THIS AS A GUIDE. Wavy hair could possibly be damaged using this. Picture Hallie Berry hair and you're fine. Usually, I don't write Amazon reviews, because the products I buy on here are ones that I don't want to pay a ton of $$ for in stores. I bought this at my local Shaws at 50% off, so around $5. I used this last night and decided, while I was waiting for my hair to dry after I washed the serum out of my hair, to take a look at reviews. I was immediately scared. I read all these reviews about how bad it was for your hair, how damaged it made seemingly healthy hair and I was immediately worried. I have healthy hair, my stylist often says she wishes people took care of my hair as I do. But, I figured, there's no turning back. So I completed all the steps and was pleasantly surprised at how NICE my hair looks. First, a few facts about my hair. I have type 3B curly hair, dark brunette that lightens when in sunshine for a couple hours. It's a long-layered reverse bob. My hair is frizzy during the summer, no matter what Ouidad I buy. I treat my hair as if it was a child, a very stubborn child. I use little to no products in my hair and only use products formulated specifically for curly hair. This includes, but is not limited to, the Garnier Fructis Sleek & Shine line, Tresemme foam-activated dry shampoo, Ouidad products and Dove Intense Moisture. My hair's drying time didn't die down a whole ton, maybe five or more minutes. But the time it took to regularly straighten my hair was practically cut in half. As I said, I did it last night, so I basically fell asleep a little afterwards and woke up late. LATE and I had to straighten? Usually, I'd just throw it up in a ponytail, but as I ran my straightener through my hair, I was relieved (and surprised) to find that it didn't take long at all. I usually don't straighten my hair, not on a regular basis anyway (the last time I did was in early May). So, I decided to tell you all how I used this product: 1.) Shampooed my hair, didn't condition. Threw it into a turbi-towel but didn't actually towel-dry (as that is HORRIBLE for curly hair). Instead, I left in my turbi-towel while I brushed my teeth/got dressed, etc. then I took it out and let it air dry. 2.) Put on those gloves and carefully put the serum into my hair. I practically got none on the scalp, I used the ponytail method to distribute it, then while I had little to no serum in my hair, would rake my hair back with my fingers. I definitely didn't use all the serum, maybe 3/4 of the bottle (I have very thick hair). 3.) Rinsed my hair out with lukewarm to warm water for a good ten minutes. Threw it up in another turbi-towel and took it down ten minutes later to air dry. BONE DRY is how you want it. 4.) Ran the lock-in moisture serum throughout my hair. It says to lightly coat it, so I did. I definitely only used a little less than half the bottle. Wondering if I could use it again after a couple washes. DO NOT use any other product with this. Don't use a heat-tamer spray or anything else. IT WILL RUIN YOUR HAIR. This product is made to act like all these. 5.) MOST IMPORTANT: You have to dry your hair before straightening. If you don't own a straightening attachment already, go out and buy one. I got mine with my Conair hair-dryer along with the diffuser. It directs the airflow into a vertical rectangle. That's what you want. You wont' get the same results without this attachment. 6.) After you blow-dry your hair completely, take your trusty flat-iron to it. As always, run it through small sections from top to bottom, not moving too quickly.it took me 1-2 tries on each section to get it to the desired 'straightness.' Poof, you're done! If you don't want to 'poo' your hair the next day, use some skinny serum (aka: Paul Mitchell's Skinny Serum, a must have for any curly-girl's shelf) and run it through your hair. I used two pumps of it each for the right side, left side, and back. Then I ran my straightener through and sprayed my hairbrush with my anti-humidity spray (Garnier's is the best) and ran that through. Again, very straight and manageable. No more of this having to practically re-straighten my hair mid-day through to get it sleek. My hair isn't damage, it's smooth and soft. My mother's already commented on how much better it looks compared to the regular straightening. The reason I give this four stars? The serum STINKS and it's a bit of a long process. (You figure 20 minutes for the serum, 20 for blow-dry, and 30-45 for straightening tacks it to about 1.5 hours thereabouts). Otherwise, i really like it. I might buy one more and keep it around until the holidays. But, so long as you stick to directions you should have no problem. :)

I think that the bad reviews are technique related. You cannot just put the product on your head, with more in some areas and less in others. You have to apply the same amount to each strand. This is an AWESOME option, if you take your time and want to save a ton of money. Yes, it's stinky. Not nearly as bad as people make it out to be.   126. I think the problem is Garnier has advertised this as being safe, non relaxer, non formaldehyde, etc.; however, there are real chemicals in this stuff. The problem with using chemicals is if a person doesn't take care of their hair during/after chemical treatment, it will feel like straw, and that person will lose their hair. By take care of it, I mean step up the conditioners: maybe a deep conditioner, maybe a leave in conditioner, maybe a bit of keratin protein, etc. It's best to continue the extra conditioning for a while after the chemical treatment, and not just on the day of. The Garnier works, and it lasts, but the only thing is, in all my years of hair straightening, and even relaxers experiments, I have never come across anything that smelled as bad as this stuff. When I read the instructions, I knew they would dry my hair out; I knew it was bogus, so here's how I did it without drying my hair out. 1. Put on dry unwashed hair for 20 minutes 2. rinse out 3. deep conditioner in the shower 4. rinse out 5. leave in conditioner 6. put on the perfect it serum and let it air dry 7. flat iron I have a combination of dry and fine hair, and it easily breaks off. That's why I use the conditioners, but if someone has oily hair, they may want to skip the leave in conditioner. Also, if someone's hair is pretty responsive to hair dryers, then they may just do that, too. My hair takes a little work, being that I'm of sicilian descent, and my curls are stubborn, so I just go straight for the flat iron. When I was done, I looked like a hair model. The effect lasted nearly two weeks (with a regimen of dry wash one day, wet wash the next). The size of these are enough to last, maybe, 6 more treatments. My hair middle of my shoulder blades, so you don't need to use a lot of this stuff. Well, I guess how much a person needs to use depends on the texture, but mine didn't need that much. Also, when I woke up the next morning, my curls were in a lovely light curl orwave. It was impressive. The stuff works, it's just Garnier didn't market it properly, and they have to do something about the smell. It doesn't go away easy; it smells just the stink bombs I got for Halloween, which is like someone leaked an SBD, a sulfuric singe your nose hairs fart on your head.

(now i know that was a chemical relaxer). then you put on what must be a keratin treatment that you have to seal onto the hair with a flat iron. it works pretty well if you want straight hair, but if you want to keep your curls, i wouldn't recommend this product. i read the entire box and it said nothing about straightening hair. it shows pictures of curly hair, it says it lasts up to 7 washes (suggesting that it will completely wash out if you don't like it), it says it's ok to use on permed hair, and it says that if you want to wear your hair curly, just not to blowdry it. it says nowhere that this product will reverse a perm, which is exactly what it did. if you have a perm you don't like, what you're supposed to do is run another perm through your hair for a few minutes without rolling it, and it will relax the perm. that's exactly what this product did to my hair. so, i recommend it if you want straight hair, but not if you like your perm.

Nor is there a warning anywhere that the use of the product as directed could cause hair breakage and loss, contend the plaintiffs.

In the morning, the texture of my hair was almost back to normal after one treatment!! Mind you, I still have broken hairs from this terrible Blow Dry stuff. The treatment can't fix that, but it does appear to be normalizing texture VERY QUICKLY compared to anything else I have tried or have read about on this site.<br />You can find the Allerga treatment online. I don't know where to get it in stores, but I'm sure it's available. I get mine from hello-gorgeous.net for $1.75 per package. I will continue to to use the protein treatment for the next little while in order to make sure I don't lose any groundwith the texture improvement. But I am very encouraged at the immediate results. Truly, my hair texture is almost normal again. Please comment on my review and let me know if it works for you too. I would love to be able to help all of the unhappy women on this product site (or coming to this site in the future) correct their sad hair as quickly as possible. It's an easy and inexpensive repair. Best of luck!!<br />Now, I have washed my hair after my \\"fix it\\" treatment, not using shampoo, just rinsing conditioner through it. I did find that I lost some of my improved texture again. Not nearly as bad as before, though. I put more of Allerga's product on and brushed through. I am thinking that a cuticle restoration product would help close the cuticle and keep the Allerga product within the cuticle better. I am looking at one on Amazon that has rave reviews. Senscience CPR Cuticle Porosity Reconstructor. Found the 2 item set for a cheaper price on sleekhair.com. I'll update my review on how it works. This one is pricey.<br />Sorry! NOTHING I have tried could repair the damage this caused. One year later, I can hold out a handful of hair and see the exact point of growth I had when I put this terrible stuff on my hair. From that area to the ends (which I have continually been cutting several inches off at a time in order to remove damage) there is a sudden decrease in volume of hair by almost half! This product truly broke off much of my hair. Additionally, although the product description says the change to your hair is temporary, and will wear off after several weeks, one year later, the hair I used this on has a very different curl appearance and texture...NOT pretty!
  232. This past weekend I was sick. Really sick. Like head-on-the-bathroom-tiles, wish-I-was-dead-because-dead-people-can't-puke sick. So Monday morning, when I finally felt better enough to not cry at the concept of eating a water cracker, I decided to perk myself up and beautify.<br /><br />Luckily (although later it would turn out to be UNLUCKILY, like cursed-for-100 years-after-breaking-77-mirrors-and-crossing-paths-with-1,000-black-cats-while-walking-under-endless-ladders unluckily), I had purchased a product that promised a \\"perfect blow dry.\\" The vials of \\"Garnier Fructis Style Sleek & Shine Blow Dry Perfector\\" were sitting on my shelf.<br /><br />I wish I had left them there. Instead, I put on the plastic gloves, which really should have been the first red flag -- what kind of hair sleek-ening product promises such silky softness and sensual smoothness that it requires you to protect your hands from it? Did I take the hint and run the other way like I should have?<br /><br />No.<br /><br />Blame the virus I just battled, or maybe blame the fact that I've been programmed to accept and submit to preposterous products and processes in the name of \\"beauty.\\" A stranger seeing my butthole before ripping out its innocent protective hairs? Yeah, sounds okay. Strapping talons to my feet? No prob! I even have friends who wear suffocating Spanx every day \\"because I feel more, well, me!\\" What?!<br /><br />So I read the instructions, which include a disclaimer along the lines of \\"it's natural for this product to have an odor.\\" I highlight my hair (another concession to beauty at the price of health and sanity -- put a zillion chemicals near my brain? Okay!) and I figured I'm used to the smell of hair products. No prob, I thought.<br /><br />I opened the vial of serum (it's a two-step process: serum and then some other goo). Words cannot describe. But for you, I'll try.<br /><br />It was like being slapped by an egg salad as it sat, vomiting, on a turd. It was like being hugged by a sea-cucumber excreting maggots who were each suffering from dysentery. It was like dying, then having your corpse worn as a corpse-hat by a haberdasher who's into that sort of thing, then having him die, and his corpse-hat-corpse being worn as a hat by his apprentice who takes over the millinery shop. It was like gout. It was like Bambi's mother's death. And then her zombie. Snacking on that skunk Flower.<br /><br />And so, I put it all over my hair.<br /><br />WHY DID I DO THIS? I don't know! Wait, I do know! Because of the above-mentioned insanity of thinking femininity somehow requires suffering, pain, and horrible, fetid, noxious smells. My best friend just revealed to me that she's gotten needles of Botox in her crows feet at 31. Crows feet she got from a teenhood addiction to tanning beds. Pain on pain, and potentially, even deeper pain from cancerous disease and disaster. But boy do the corners of her eyes look like a baby's bottom!<br /><br />At one point, my cat came into the bathroom, where I was standing with a towel draped around my neck, because the package advised that I might not want to let this stuff touch my skin. (Another red flag I insanely did not recognize.) Mind you, he's a vocal cat, and sensitive to smells -- like when he smells salad dressing, his blue eyes close up like he's a furry little feline stoner -- but he shot out of the bathroom yowling.<br /><br />Yowling.<br /><br />Soon, I would be too. As I dipped into the shower after sitting for 20 minutes with the stuff -- because, I figured, once I had this regurgitated-egg-yolk, fish feces, goat entrails potion on my head, I might as well grit and bear it for the recommended time -- I touched, at last, my hair.<br /><br />It felt like the sun bleached hayfields of a Monet painting. It felt like the Brillo pad that's been crusting and rusting to the edge of my sink. It felt like Garth Algar's coif after a trip through the Serengeti. It felt like pain. No, wrath.<br /><br />I actuallyscreamed \\"What have I done?\\" to no one, while bent over the tub.<br /><br />I washed it out again, and still my head stank. I opened the windows. I moaned like Ludo in Labyrinth, my favorite movie, when he gets sent to the Bog of Eternal Stench and has to step over the rocks that jut up out of the murk, and every time he treads on one it emits wild, popping farts.<br /><br />Only the bog was my hair.<br /><br />On the Garnier website, there are a number of positive reviews for this product, presumably from people who a) hate themselves, b) hate other people, c) are insane, d) cannot smell, e) cannot feel texture, or f) all of the above, in which case, I really do forgive them for writing those reviews, because that sounds like a tough life.<br /><br />But below the handful of positive reviews from insane-os are scores of real reviews. A sampling:<br /><br /> SaraW: \\"The instructions warn there will be an odor but the smell was so much worse than I ever thought it would be.\\"<br /> Maki418: \\"The smell is horrible and it will not go away. I've washed my hair over and over and it still smells. Now my hair is like rubber.\\"<br /> KimMie88: \\"It smells so bad my husband had to leave the house.\\"<br /> KimV: \\"The only way I can describe it is like if you put NAIR on it and washed it out before it completely melted it\\"<br /> MAD1: \\"can't even comb my hair it looks like and old piece of carpet!\\"<br /><br />And that's on the company website! Amazon has more horror stories.<br /><br />So I sprayed a billion spritzes of perfume into my hair while I styled it with a blowdyer and a straightening iron, and in the end it looked exactly like it always does after I blow-dry and straighten it, with the main difference being that it feels one zillion times worse and smells like death.<br /><br />To top if off, my eyes sting from where I spritzed them (the instructions say to go to the hospital if you get it in your eyes, FYI, but the funny thing is that your hair is right next to your eyes), and I now have old woman fingers where I accidentally got some on me. Like crone-style, which kind of matches my odor, so at least I have consistency going for me.<br /><br />Am I a victim of my own vanity? Hells yes. But are the people at Garnier at least partially responsible for marketing a product like this to women under such a fuzzy name as \\"blow-dry perfector\\" rather than the chemical slop of<br /><br /> water, Cysteine, Ethanolamine*, PEG-14 Dimethicone, Hexadimethrine Chloride, Aminomethyl Propanol, Polysorbate 20, Oleth-20, Hydroxyethylcellulose, Hydroxypropyl Guar, Cetrimonium Chloride, Dimethicone PEG-7 Phosphate, Parfum/Fragrance, Pentasodium Pentetate.<br /><br />(*Ethanolamine, by the by, according to the Occupational Safety and Health Administration of the United States Department of Labor, causes \\"central nervous system depression in exposed animals\\" at certain levels, and don't even get me started on Hexadimethrine Chloride.)<br /><br />But a more appropriate point of blame would be assenting to the notion held by many -- myself included -- that beauty is pain, pain beauty. (Note they never say that about \\"handsomeness.\\") That concept is what allowed this disgusting product to exist, and what made me slather it on my head. Even my already brutalized stomach flipped and flopped a resounding \\"don't do it! Please dear God don't do it!\\"<br /><br />My hair -- and the colleagues who sit by my cubicle and have been hit by its wafting stench with the ferocity of a cartoon hand symbolizing \\"stink\\" every few minutes -- are the worse for this morning's mistake. But I think, maybe, I'm for the better.<br /><br />[...]ank. I opened the windows.   235. I figured out this product. This is a relaxer. Look up the main ingredient Cysteine and you will see it contains sulfur. It is part of the Thiol group. So what you are experiencing is the chemical break down of your hair. The effect would be less if there were a neutralizer as a product sold as a relaxer does. However not only are you putting a chemical that breaks down the bond of your hair without neutralization, but then you apply heat to it another process that breaks the chemical bond of your hair. This is negligent at best because it is a chemical that is not regulated...relaxers. The &#34;black&#34; community has been subjected to these damaging products and no one regulates them. I doubt anyone ever will regulate it because they make too much money. It now has crossed over into an industry that promotes &#34;managing&#34; curly hair and relentless advertising to straighten hair. Two solutions for those with damage. Cut off the ends and apply raw shea butter. Buy some shea butter from an African food store. Shea butter has healing properties. Also for the hair broken at the root continue to apply the shea butter and trim it as is grows out. Be patient. Your hair will grow back. A second solution for the brave would be to shave your head or buzz cut it and wear a wig. This would be faster in that it would get rid of all the chemical damage. This is what women in the Natural Hair Movement have been doing. My African sisters and/or curly hair sisters have been doing this to return to natural after relaxing their hair for years (decades). Peace!

Basically how it works is first, wash your hair but don't apply any conditioner. Use the gloves provided and apply tube #1 which is a &#34;20 minute Smooth-It Serum&#34;, and keep hair as straight as you can while it's processing. The product in this tube smells like sulphur to a pretty profound degree, enough to be bothersome for some people I am sure, however, you need not worry, you won't smell it in your hair after completion.<br /><br />Next you are going to rinse the 20 minute Smooth-It Serum with warm water and apply tube #2 &#34;Heat Activated Perfect-It Cream&#34; which acts as a sort of sealer. This application doesn't get rinsed out, it stays in, you then blow dry and flat iron and you're done! This tube has a pleasant scent to it.<br /><br />After you follow these steps to completion be prepared to love your hair!
